<P STYLE="font: 11pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 5.4pt 0 0; text-
align: center"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif"><B>DYNARESOURCE,

<P STYLE="font: 11pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0; text-align: 
center"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; text-transform: 
uppercase"><B>Notes
to the UNAUDITED Consolidated Financial Statements</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 12pt; text-
align: center"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>June
30, 2015 and 2014</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B><U>NOTE
1 &#8211; NATURE OF OPERATIONS AND BASIS OF PRESENTATION</U></B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">DynaResource,
Inc. (The &#8220;Company&#8221;, &#8220;DynaResource&#8221;, or 
&#8220;DynaUSA&#8221;) was organized September 28, 1937, as a
California corporation under the name of West Coast Mines, Inc.&nbsp;&nbsp;In 
1998, the Company re-domiciled to Delaware and changed
its name to DynaResource, Inc.&nbsp;The Company is in the business of acquiring,
investing in, and developing precious metal properties,
and the pilot production of precious metals.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
interim consolidated financial statements included herein have been prepared by 
the Company, without audit, pursuant to the rules&nbsp;and
regulations of the Securities and Exchange Commission (&#8220;SEC&#8221;).&nbsp;
Certain information and note disclosures normally
included in financial statements prepared in accordance with accounting 
principles generally accepted in the United States of
America (&#8220;U.S. GAAP&#8221;) has been condensed or omitted pursuant to such
rules&nbsp;and regulations, although the Company
believes that the disclosures included are adequate to make the information 
presented not misleading.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">In
management&#8217;s opinion, the unaudited Consolidated Statements of Operations 
and Comprehensive Income for the three and six
months ended June 30, 2015 and 2014, the Consolidated Balance Sheets as of June 
30, 2015 (unaudited) and December&nbsp;31, 2014,
and the unaudited Consolidated Statements of Cash Flows for the six months ended
June 30, 2015 and 2014, contained herein, reflect
all adjustments, consisting solely of normal recurring items, which are 
necessary for the fair presentation of the Company&#8217;s
financial position, results of operations and cash flows on a basis consistent 
with that of the Company&#8217;s prior audited
annual consolidated financial statements.&nbsp; However, the results of 
operations for the interim periods may not be indicative
of results to be expected for the full fiscal year.&nbsp; Therefore these 
financial statements should be read in conjunction with
the audited financial statements and notes thereto and summary of significant 
accounting policies included in the Company&#8217;s
Form&nbsp;10-K for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2014.&nbsp; Except as noted 
below, there have been no material changes in
the footnotes from those accompanying the audited consolidated financial 
statements contained in the Company&#8217;s Form&nbsp;10-K
for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2014. The consolidated financial statements
include the accounts of the Company and its wholly-owned
subsidiaries.&nbsp; All inter-company accounts and transactions have been 
eliminated.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 12pt; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">Certain
amounts for the three and six month periods ending June 30, 2014 have been 
adjusted to current reporting format.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B><U>NOTE
2 &#8211; INVESTMENT IN AFFILIATE/RECEIVABLES FROM AFFILIATE/OTHER 
ASSETS</U></B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 12pt; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif">DynaResource
Nevada, Inc., a Nevada Corporation (&#8220;DynaNevada&#8221;), with one 
operating subsidiary in M&eacute;xico, DynaNevada de M&eacute;xico,
S.A. de C.V. (&#8220;DynaNevada de M&eacute;xico&#8221;) have common officers, 
directors and shareholders with the Company. The
total amount loaned by the Company to DynaNevada at December 31, 2010 was 
$805,760. The terms of the Note Receivable provided
for a &#8220;Convertible Loan,&#8221; repayable at 5% interest over a 3 year 
period, and convertible at the Company&#8217;s option
into Common Stock of DynaNevada at $0.25 / Share.&nbsp;&nbsp;On December 31, 
2010, the Company converted its receivable from DynaNevada
into 3,223,040 Shares of DynaNevada; and as a result, the Company owns 19.92% of
the outstanding share capital of DynaNevada.
DynaNevada is a related entity, and through its subsidiary in M&eacute;xico 
(DynaNevada de M&eacute;xico), (&#8220;DynaNevada
de M&eacute;xico&#8221;), entered into an Option agreement with Grupo 
M&eacute;xico (&#8220;IMMSA&#8221;) in M&eacute;xico, for
the exploration and development of approximately 3,000 hectares in the State of 
San Luis Potosi (&#8220;the Santa Gertrudis Property&#8221;).
In March, 2010, DynaNevada de M&eacute;xico completed the Option with IMMSA so 
that it now owns 100% of Santa Gertrudis. In June,
2010, DynaNevada de M&eacute;xico acquired an additional 6,000 Hectares in the 
State of Sinaloa (&#8220;the San Juan Property&#8221;).
The Company has loaned additional funds to DynaNevada since 2010 for maintenance
of concessions and other nominal required fees
and expenses. The Company currently has a receivable from DynaResource Nevada, 
Inc. of $167,666 and an investment balance of $70,000
as of June 30, 2015. The balances as of December 31, 2014 were $172,968 in 
receivables and $70,000 in investment, respectively.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B><U>NOTE
3 &#8211; PROMISSORY NOTES</U></B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt"><FONT 
STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Notes
Payable &#8211; Series I</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">In
April and May, 2013, the Company entered into note agreements with individual 
shareholders in the principal amount of $1,495,000,
of which $340,000 was then converted to Series B Preferred shares within the 
same year, netting to proceeds of $1,155,000 (the
&#8220;Series I Notes&#8221; Series I). The Series I Notes bear simple interest 
at twelve and a half percent (12.5%), accrued
interest for twelve months, and with&nbsp;the accrued interest to be 
added&nbsp;to the principal, and then interest to be paid
by the Company,&nbsp;quarterly in arrears. The holders of the Series I Notes (in
aggregate) are also entitled to&nbsp;receive
ten percent (10%) of the net profits received by the Company, and&nbsp;generated
from the bulk sampling material (if any, and&nbsp;up
to fifty thousand tonnes) processed through the existing, or improved mill 
facilities at San Jose de Gracia. Such net profits
(if any) are to&nbsp;be calculated after deducting all expenses related to the 
processing of the bulk sample material,&nbsp;and
after a prior&nbsp;deduction of&nbsp;thirty three percent (33%) from the 
profits, to be deposited in a sinking fund cash reserve.
This net profit percentage (if any) would&nbsp;be paid quarterly in arrears 
based on the profits generated (if any)&nbsp;for the
prior quarter. At the time of the Series I Notes, there were no proven or 
probable reserves and the Company had not produced any
net profits. Consequently, the fair value of the net profits interest on the 
date of the Series I Note was deemed to be zero.
Further, no payments have been made under the terms of this codicil. The Notes 
originally matured on December 31, 2015. In April,
2015, the notes were extended to December 31, 2016.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Company has the right to prepay the Series I Notes with a ten percent (10%) 
penalty. The notes are secured by the Company&#8217;s
stock at $5 per share.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"></FONT></P>
<!-- Field: Page; Sequence: 7 -->
    <DIV STYLE="margin-top: 12pt; margin-bottom: 6pt; border-bottom: Black 1pt 
solid"><TABLE CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" STYLE="border-collapse: collapse; 
width: 100%; font-size: 10pt"><TR STYLE="vertical-align: top; text-align: 
left"><TD STYLE="width: 100%; text-align: right"><!-- Field: Sequence; Type: 
Arabic; Name: PageNo -->7<!-- Field: /Sequence --></TD></TR></TABLE></DIV>
    <DIV STYLE="page-break-before: always; margin-top: 6pt; margin-bottom: 
12pt">&nbsp;</DIV>
    <!-- Field: /Page -->
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Series I Note holder retains the option, at any time prior to maturity or 
prepayment, to convert any unpaid principal and accrued
interest into Common Stock at $5.00 per share. If the Series I Note is converted
into Common Stock, at the time of conversion,
the holder would also receive warrants, in the same number as the number of 
common shares received upon conversion, to purchase
additional common shares of the Company for $7.50 per share, with such warrants 
expiring on December 31, 2015. In 2013, the Company
offered an inducement to all Series I Note holders to convert their Series I 
Notes and accrued interest into Series B Preferred
Stock (&#8220;Series B&#8221;), $5/Share, which Series B was convertible into 
common stock on a 2 for 1 basis (i.e., $2.50 stock).
This conversion into Series B created $197,771 in inducement expense, with an 
offset to additional paid in capital. In 2013, $340,000
principal and $22,734 of capitalized accrued interest of the Series I Notes were
converted into Preferred Stock, Series B and
72,546 shares were issued. At June 30, 2014, these 72,546 Series B shares were 
converted into 145,092 common shares.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">In
April, 2015, the Company received note extensions (allonges) from all Series I 
note holders to ensure that all Series I Notes
were in good standing and it also extended the maturity date of the Series I 
Notes to December 31, 2016.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Notes
Payable &#8211; Series II</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">In
2013 and 2014, the Company entered into additional note agreements of $199,808 
and $250,000, respectively (the &#8220;Series II
Notes&#8221;) with similar terms as the Series I notes. The Series II Notes bear
simple interest at twelve and a half percent
(12.5%), accrued for twelve months, and with&nbsp;the accrued interest to be 
added&nbsp;to the principal, and then interest will
be paid by the Company,&nbsp;quarterly in arrears. The holders of the Series II 
Notes (in aggregate) are also entitled to&nbsp;receive
ten percent (10%) of the net profits received by the Company, and&nbsp;generated
from the bulk sampling material (if any, on the
second fifty thousand tonnes) processed through the existing, or improved mill 
facilities at San Jose de Gracia. Such net profits
(if any) are to&nbsp;be calculated after deducting all expenses related to the 
processing of the bulk sample material,&nbsp;and
after a prior&nbsp;deduction of&nbsp;thirty three percent (33%) from the 
profits, to be deposited in a sinking fund cash reserve.
This net profit percentage (if any) would&nbsp;be paid quarterly in arrears 
based on the profits generated (if any)&nbsp;for the
prior quarter. At the time of the Series II notes, there were no proven or 
probable reserves and the Company had not produced
any net profits. Consequently, the fair value of the net profits interest on the
date of the Series II note was deemed to be zero.
Further, no payments have been made under the terms of this codicil. The Notes 
mature on December 31, 2016.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Company has the right to prepay the Notes with a ten percent (10%) penalty. The 
notes are secured by the Company&#8217;s stock
at $5 per share.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Note holder may, at any time prior to maturity or prepayment, convert any unpaid
principal and accrued interest into common stock
of the Company at $5.00 per share. At the time of conversion, the holder would 
receive a warrant to purchase additional common
shares of the Company for $7.50 per share, such warrant expiring on December 31,
2016.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Series
I and Series II Notes Outstanding</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The

as of June 30, 2015 and December 31, 2014, respectively.

2015 and December 31, 2014, respectively. The principal
balance on the Note&#8212;Related Party was $0 and $250,000 as of June 30, 2015 
and December 31, 2014, respectively.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:

noteholders to ensure that all notes were in good standing
and also confirmed the maturity of the Series II notes to be December 31,
2016.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:

<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B><U>NOTE
7 &#8211; COMMITMENTS AND CONTINGENCIES</U></B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Company is required to pay taxes in M&eacute;xico in order to maintain mining 
concessions owned by DynaM&eacute;xico.&nbsp;&nbsp;Additionally,
the Company is required to incur a minimum amount of expenditures each year for 
all concessions held.&nbsp;&nbsp;The minimum expenditures
are calculated based upon the land area, as well as the age of the
concessions.&nbsp;&nbsp;Amounts spent in excess of the minimum
may be carried forward indefinitely over the life of the concessions, and are 
adjusted annually for inflation.&nbsp;&nbsp;Based
on Management&#8217;s business plans, the Company does not anticipate that 
DynaM&eacute;xico will have any issues in meeting the
minimum annual expenditures for the concessions, and DynaM&eacute;xico retains 
sufficient carry-forward amounts to cover over
20 years of the minimum expenditure (as calculated at the 2014 minimum, adjusted
for annual inflation of 4%).</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; letter-spacing: 
-0.1pt">In
addition to the surface rights held by DynaM&eacute;xico pursuant to the 
<I>Mining Act</I> of M&eacute;xico and its Regulations
(<I>Ley Minera y su Reglamento</I>), DynaMineras maintains access and surface 
rights to the SJG Project pursuant to a 20 year
Land Lease Agreement with the Santa Maria Ejido community adjacent to San Jose 
de Gracia.</FONT><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">
The <FONT STYLE="background-color: white">20 Year Land Lease Agreement with the 
Santa Maria Ejido was dated January 6, 2014 and
continues through 2033. It covers an area of 4,399 hectares surrounding the main
mineral resource areas of SJG, and provides for
annual lease payments by DynaMineras of $1,359,443 Pesos (approx. $85,000 USD), 
commencing in 2014. </FONT>The Land Lease Agreement
provides DynaMineras with surface access to the core resource areas of SJG 
(4,399 hectares), and allows for all permitted mining
and exploration activities from the owners of the surface rights (Santa Maria 
Ejido community).</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">In
September 2008, the Company entered into a 37 month lease agreement for its 
corporate office.&nbsp;&nbsp;In June, 2015, the Company
entered into a one-year extension of the lease through August 31, 2016. The 
Company paid rent expense of $31,234 and $25,000 related
to this lease for the six months ended June 30, 2015 and 2014, 
respectively.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt 10pt; text-
align: justify; text-indent: -10pt"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, 
Times, Serif"><B>Other
Contingencies </B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Company's mining and exploration activities are subject to various laws and 
regulations governing the protection of the environment.
These laws and regulations are continually changing and generally becoming more 
restrictive. The Company conducts its operations
so as to protect public health and the environment, and believes its operations 
are materially in compliance with all applicable
laws and regulations. The Company has made, and expects to make in the future, 
expenditures to comply with such laws and regulations.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif"><B>Litigation</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 10pt; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Company believes that no material adverse change will occur as a result of the 
legal actions taken, and the Company further believes
that there is little to no potential for the assessment of a material monetary
judgment against the Company for legal actions
it has filed in M&eacute;xico. Further, the Company believes there is no legal 
basis for which to conduct arbitration proceedings.
(See Item 2. Management&#8217;s Discussion and Analysis of Financial Conditions 
and Results of Operations; and see Part II, Item
1. Legal Proceedings.)</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:

<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:

9 &#8211; SUBSEQUENT EVENTS</U></B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 12pt; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">On
July 1, 2015, the Company received $3,500,000 (less costs of $108,800), from 
Golden Post Rail LLC, as described in Note 4 above.</FONT></P>
<TABLE CELLSPACING="0" CELLPADDING="0" STYLE="font: 8pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif; width: 100%">
<TR STYLE="vertical-align: top">
    <TD STYLE="padding-bottom: 6pt; font-size: 10pt; text-decoration: underline;
text-align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif"><B><U>NOTE
    10 &#8211; FAIR VALUE OF FINANCIAL INSTRUMENTS</U></B></FONT></TD></TR>
</TABLE>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
ASC guidance for fair value measurements and disclosure establishes a fair value
hierarchy that prioritizes the inputs to valuation
techniques used to measure fair value. The hierarchy gives the highest priority 
to unadjusted quoted prices in active markets
for identical assets or liabilities (Level 1 measurements) and the lowest 
priority to unobservable inputs (Level 3 measurements).&nbsp;&nbsp;The
three levels of the fair value hierarchy are described below:</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt 0.5in; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><I>Level
1 Inputs</I> &#8211; Quoted prices for identical instruments in active 
markets.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt 0.5in; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><I>Level
2 Inputs</I> &#8211; Quoted prices for similar instruments in active markets; 
quoted prices for identical or similar instruments
in markets that are not active; and model-derived valuations whose inputs are 
observable or whose significant value drivers are
observable.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt 0.5in; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><I>Level
3 Inputs</I> &#8211; Instruments with primarily unobservable value 
drivers.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">As
of June 30, 2015 and 2014, carrying value of the Company&#8217;s financial 
assets and liabilities, such as cash, receivables,
inventories approximate fair value because of their short maturity. The 
derivative liabilities are measured at fair value using
quoted market prices and estimated volatility factors based on historical quoted
market prices for the Company&#8217;s common
stock and are classified within Level 3 of the valuation hierarchy.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 8pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0; text-align: 
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Fair
Value Measurement at June 30, 2015 Using:</B></FONT></P>

assumptions, including but not limited to, risks, uncertainties

contribute to these differences include those described
under the heading &#8220;Management Discussion and Analysis and Plan of 
Operation.&#8221;</FONT></P>

<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>CAUTIONARY
NOTE TO UNITED STATES INVESTORS&#8212;INFORMATION CONCERNING PREPARATION OF 
RESOURCE AND RESERVE ESTIMATES </B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Company is an &#8220;OTC Reporting Issuer&#8221; as that term is defined in BC 
Multilateral Instrument 51-105, <I>Issuers Quoted
in the U.S. Over-the-Counter Markets</I>, promulgated by the British Columbia 
Securities Commission. Accordingly, certain disclosure
in this quarterly report has been prepared in accordance with the requirements 
of securities laws in effect in Canada, which differ
from the requirements of United States securities laws. In Canada, an issuer is 
required to provide technical information with
respect to mineralization, including reserves and resources, if any, on its 
mineral exploration properties in accordance with
Canadian requirements, which differ significantly from the requirements of the 
United States Securities and Exchange Commission
(the &#8220;SEC&#8221;) applicable to registration statements and reports filed 
by United States companies pursuant to the Securities
Act or the Exchange Act. As such, information contained in this annual report 
concerning descriptions of mineralization under
Canadian standards may not be comparable to similar information made public by 
United States companies subject to the reporting
and disclosure requirements of the SEC and not subject to Canadian securities 
legislation. This annual report may use the terms
&#8220;measured mineral resources&#8221;, &#8220;indicated mineral 
resources&#8221; and &#8220;inferred mineral resources&#8221;.
While these terms are recognized and required by Canadian securities legislation
(under National Instrument 43-101, <I>Standards
of Disclosure for Mineral Projects</I>), the SEC does not recognize them. United
States investors are cautioned not to assume
that any part or all of the mineral deposits in these categories will ever be 
converted to reserves. In addition, &#8220;inferred
mineral resources&#8221; have a great amount of uncertainty as to their 
existence and economic and legal feasibility. It cannot
be assumed that all or any part of a measured mineral resource, indicated 
mineral resource or inferred mineral resource will ever
be upgraded to a higher category. Under Canadian securities legislation, 
estimates of inferred mineral resources may not form
the basis of feasibility or pre-feasibility studies, although they may form, in 
certain circumstances, the basis of a &#8220;preliminary
economic assessment&#8221; as that term is defined in National Instrument 43-
101, <I>Standards of Disclosure for Mineral Projects</I>.
U.S. investors are cautioned not to assume that any part or all of any reported 
measured, indicated, or inferred mineral resource
estimates referred to herein or in the Technical Report are economically or 
legally mineable.</FONT></P>

    <DIV STYLE="margin-top: 12pt; margin-bottom: 6pt; border-bottom: Black 1pt

<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify">&nbsp;</P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif"><B>Company</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Company is a minerals investment, management, and exploration company, and 
currently conducting test mining and pilot milling
operations through an operating subsidiary in M&eacute;xico, with specific focus
on precious and base metals in M&eacute;xico.
The Company was incorporated in the State of California on September 28, 1937, 
under the name West Coast Mines, Inc. In November
1998, the Company re-domiciled from California to Delaware and changed its name 
to DynaResource, Inc. (&#8220;DynaUSA&#8221;).</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">In
2000, the Company formed DynaResource de M&eacute;xico S.A. de C.V. 
(&#8220;DynaM&eacute;xico&#8221;) for the purpose of acquiring
and holding mineral properties and mining concessions in M&eacute;xico and, 
specifically for acquiring and consolidating the Mining
District of San Jose de Gracia. DynaM&eacute;xico completed the consolidation of
the entire SJG District to DynaM&eacute;xico
in 2003 (approx. 15 sq. km. at that time), with the exception of the San Miguel 
Mining Concession (7 Hectares, for which DynaM&eacute;xico
is proceeding towards accomplishing the transfer of title, under previously 
signed sale and purchase agreements).</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif">DynaM&eacute;xico
currently owns a portfolio of mining concessions, equipment, camp and related 
facilities which comprise the San Jos&eacute; de
Gracia Project (&#8220;SJG&#8221;). The mining concessions cover 69,121 hectares
(170,802 acres) on the west side of the Sierra
Madre mountain range, in northern Sinaloa State.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Company currently owns 80% of the outstanding shares of DynaM&eacute;xico. We 
also own 100% of Mineras de DynaResource S.A. de
C.V. (&#8220;DynaMineras&#8221;), the exclusive operator of the San Jos&eacute; 
de Gracia Project, under contract with DynaM&eacute;xico,
and we own 100% of DynaResource Operaciones de San Jose de Gracia, S.A. de C.V.,
(&#8220;DynaOperaciones&#8221;), a company which
manages the personnel registered to work at the San Jose de Gracia 
Project.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt/12pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>San
Jose de Gracia - History</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt/12pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif">Historical
production records from San Jose de Gracia (&#8220;SJG&#8221;) report 1,000,000 
Oz gold production from a series of underground
workings. The major areas report 471,000 Oz. produced at the La Purisima area of
SJG, at an average grade of 66.7 g/t.; and 215,000
Oz. produced from the La Prieta area, at an average grade of 27.6 g/t. 
Mineralization at SJG has been traced on surface and underground
over 15 sq. km.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt/12pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif">DynaM&eacute;xico
was formed in March 2000, for the purpose of acquiring the concessions 
comprising the SJG District, and to consolidate all ownership
of SJG under DynaM&eacute;xico. DynaM&eacute;xico focused on acquisition and 
consolidation work through 2003, and reported a virtually
clear title and consolidated ownership to the district at December 31, 
2013.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Drilling
&#8211; Exploration Programs (1997 &#8211; 2000)</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">A
drill program was conducted at SJG in 1997 to 1998 by a prior majority owner. 
Approximately 6,172 meters drilling was completed
in 63 core drill holes. Significant intercepts, including bonanza grades, 
outlined the down dip potential of the Northeast section
(150 Meter NE to SW extent of the Drilling) of the Los Hilos to Tres Amigos 
Trend of SJG. Surface and underground sampling in
1999 to 2000 confirmed high grades in historic workings and surface exposures 
throughout the project area. These high grades outline
the presence of mineralization shoots developed within the veins.&nbsp;The 
mineralized shoots appear to be controlled by dilational
jogs and/or vein intersections. A total of 544 samples were collected in 1999 to
2000, and assayed an average 6.51 g/t gold.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Structure
of Company / Operations</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">Activities
in M&eacute;xico are currently conducted by DynaMineras; with the management of 
personnel being contracted by DynaMineras through
to DynaOperaciones. Management of DynaResource, Inc. and consultants manage the 
operating companies in M&eacute;xico; while the
Chairman/CEO of DynaUSA is the President of each of DynaM&eacute;xico, 
DynaMineras and DynaOperaciones. Fees for management and
administration are charged by DynaMineras and DynaOperaciones, which are 
eliminated in consolidation.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0.3in 6pt 0; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif"><B>Exclusive
Operating Entity at San Jose de Gracia</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">Under
agreement with DynaM&eacute;xico, Mineras de DynaResource S.A. de C.V. 
(&#8220;DynaMineras&#8221;) has been named the exclusive
operating entity at the San Jose de Gracia Project. DynaResource owns 100% of 
DynaMineras.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif"><B>DynaM&eacute;xico
General Powers of Attorney</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Chairman-CEO of DynaUSA also serves as the President of DynaM&eacute;xico. The 
President of DynaM&eacute;xico holds broad powers
of attorney granted by the shareholders of DynaM&eacute;xico which gives the 
current President significant and broad authority
within DynaM&eacute;xico.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:

<P STYLE="font: 10pt/13pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Pilot
Production Activities (2003 &#8211; 2006)</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt/13pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif">DynaM&eacute;xico,
conducting operations through DynaMineras, mined high-grade veins at the San 
Pablo area of SJG from mid-2003 to June 2006. 18,250
Oz. gold was produced and sold from mill feed tonnage of 42,000 tonnes, at an 
average grade of approximately 15-20 g/t. Production
costs were reported at approximately $175/Oz. gold in this small scale, pilot 
production operation (See results in table below).
The pilot operations at SJG consisted of the installation of a gravity/flotation
processing circuit to an existing mill, and initial
test runs with tailings were completed in 2002. Actual test mining at the higher
grade San Pablo area of the property commenced
in March 2003.</FONT></P>

<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 6pt 0"><FONT 
STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Suspension
of Production Activities (2006)</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt/12pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Company initiated the test production activity in 2003 and, at that time, gold 
prices were depressed. Exploration funding opportunities,
while available, were deemed to be too dilutive by Company management. 
Subsequently, in 2006, commodities prices were improving
and the Company was able to negotiate financing in order to fund exploration 
activities. Therefore, the Company suspended test
mining activities in 2006 in order to focus on the exploration of the vast SJG 
District. While the test mining and pilot milling
operations were considered successful (see results in the table above), a small 
scale production operation was not expected to
provide the necessary capital in order to fund exploration of the vast SJG 
District. The limited-scope pilot production activity
provided significant benefits through confirmation of production grades, 
metallurgy and process, efficiency of recoveries, and
production costs.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt/12pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif"><B>Drilling
programs (2007 &#8211; 2011)</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin-top: 0; margin-
bottom: 6pt; margin-left: 0pt; text-indent: 0pt; text-align: justify"><FONT 
STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">Drilling
programs completed by the Company&#8217;s subsidiaries produced a total of 298 
drill holes covering 68,741 meters of drilling
from 2007 through March 2011. Results of the drilling activity, including the 
results of previous drilling in 1997-1998, appear
in an &#8220;SJG Drill Intercepts Summary File through 11-298&#8221;, as Exhibit
99.1 to our Form 10-Q for the period ended June
30, 2011 filed with the SEC on August 22, 2011, and available on EDGAR at: 
[http://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1111741/000112178111000241/ex99one.htm].
Additionally, the updated Drill Summary File is posted on the Company&#8217;s 
web site at www.dynaresource.com.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt"><FONT 
STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Mineral
Resource Estimate and Technical Report 43-101 (2012)</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">In
2012, DynaM&eacute;xico commissioned <FONT STYLE="background-color: 
white">Servicios y Proyectos Mineros</FONT> (&#8220;SPM&#8221;)
for the production of Technical Report 43-101 (&#8220;43-101&#8221;) at San Jose
de Gracia. Additionally, DynaM&eacute;xico commissioned
Mr. Robert Sandefur, a senior reserve analyst for Chlumsky, Armbrust &amp; Meyer
LLC, Lakewood, CO (&#8220;CAM&#8221;) to produce
a mineral resource estimate for the 4 main vein systems at the 
property.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><I>Parameters
Used to Estimate the Mineral Resource Estimate--</I>The data base for the San 
Jose de Gracia Project consists of 372 drill holes
of which 361 are diamond drill holes (&#8220;DDH&#8221;) and the remaining 11 
were reverse circulation holes &#8220;(RC&#8221;),
with a total drilling of 75,878 meters. The 2012 DynaM&eacute;xico-CAM SJG 
Mineral Resource Estimate concentrates on four main
mineralized vein systems at SJG: Tres Amigos, San Pablo, La Union, and La 
Purisima. Of the 372 drill holes, 368 were drilled to
test these four main vein systems and the remaining four holes tested the 
Argillic Zone. Technical personnel of Minop S.A. de
C.V. (&#8220;Minop&#8221;), a subsidiary (or affiliate) of Goldgroup Mining Inc.
(&#8220;Goldgroup&#8221;) built three dimensional
solids to constrain estimation to the interpreted veins in each swarm. The 172 
holes most recently drilled (2009-2011), were allocated
as follows: Tres Amigos (64 holes), San Pablo (49 holes), La Union (24 holes), 
La Purisima (32 holes) and Argillic Zone (3 holes).
The data base also includes rock and chip sampling, regional stream sediment 
sampling, and IP Surveys.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><I>Density--
</I>A
total of 5,540 pieces of core were measured for specific gravity using the 
weight in air vs. weight in water method. This represents
an additional 3,897 measurements taken in the 2009-11 drill seasons with density
measurements taken from all mineral zones. Dried
samples were coated with paraffin wax before being measured. The results 
tabulated have been sorted by lithology and mineralized
veins. The average specific gravity of 5,051 wall rock samples was 2.59 while 
the average specific gravity for 489 samples of
vein material is 2.68. CAM and Servicios y Proyectos Mineros have reviewed the 
procedures and results, and opine that the results
are suitable for use in mineral resource estimation.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><I>Mineral
Resource Estimate - Construction of Wireframes--</I>Mineral Resources were 
estimated by Mr. Sandefur within wireframes constructed
by technical personnel of Minop. Minop was contracted by Mineras de DynaResource
S.A. de C.V. (&#8220;DynaMineras&#8221;).</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"></P>
<!-- Field: Page; Sequence: 14 -->
    <DIV STYLE="margin-top: 12pt; margin-bottom: 6pt; border-bottom: Black 1pt 
solid"><TABLE CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" STYLE="border-collapse: collapse; 
width: 100%; font-size: 10pt"><TR STYLE="vertical-align: top; text-align: 
left"><TD STYLE="width: 100%; text-align: right"><!-- Field: Sequence; Type: 
Arabic; Name: PageNo -->14<!-- Field: /Sequence --></TD></TR></TABLE></DIV>
    <DIV STYLE="page-break-before: always; margin-top: 6pt; margin-bottom: 
12pt">&nbsp;</DIV>
    <!-- Field: /Page -->
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify">&nbsp;</P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><I>Mineral
Resource Estimate - Explanation of Resource Estimation--</I>Resource estimation 
was done in MineSight and MicroModel computer
systems with only those composites that were inside the wireframe used in the 
estimate. Estimation was done using kriging with
the omni-directional variogram derived from all the data in each area for gold 
using the relative variogram derived from the log
variogram. High grades were restricted by capping the assays at a breakpoint 
based on the cumulative frequency curves. Estimation
was done using search radii of 100 x 100 x 50 m &#8220;blocks&#8221; oriented 
subparallel to the general strike and dip of the
vein system in each area. A sector search, corresponding to the faces of the 
search box with a maximum of two points per sector
was used in estimation. A density of 2.68 based on within &#8216;vein 
density&#8217; samples was used in the resource estimate.
Within each of the four areas there are approximately 20 to 40 veins in the vein
swarm. Resources were estimated by kriging using
data from all veins in the swarm. In general, gold accounts for at least 80% of 
the value of contained metal at the project, so
the variograms for gold were used in estimation of the four other metals. 
Mineral Resources at Tres Amigos&nbsp;and San Pablo
were classified as &#8220;Indicated&#8221; as follows:</FONT></P>
<TABLE CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%" STYLE="font: 10pt Times New 
Roman, Times, Serif; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0"><TR STYLE="vertical-align:
top">
<TD STYLE="width: 0.75in"></TD><TD STYLE="width: 0.25in"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt
Times New Roman, Times, Serif">1)</FONT></TD><TD STYLE="text-align: 
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">they
                                         were within a vein within the swarm 
which contained at least 7 drill holes;</FONT></TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%" STYLE="font: 10pt Times New 
Roman, Times, Serif; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 6pt"><TR STYLE="vertical-
align: top">
<TD STYLE="width: 0.75in"></TD><TD STYLE="width: 0.25in"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt
Times New Roman, Times, Serif">2)</FONT></TD><TD STYLE="text-align: 
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">they
                                         are within 25 m of the nearest sample 
point; and,</FONT></TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%" STYLE="font: 10pt Times New 
Roman, Times, Serif; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 6pt"><TR STYLE="vertical-
align: top">
<TD STYLE="width: 0.75in"></TD><TD STYLE="width: 0.25in"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt
Times New Roman, Times, Serif">3)</FONT></TD><TD STYLE="text-align: 
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">the
                                         block was estimated by at least three 
drill holes.</FONT></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 6pt 0; text-align: 
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">All
other Mineral Resources were classified as &#8220;Inferred&#8221;. Since there 
are no precise quantitative definitions of Measured,
Indicated and Inferred, resource classification is subjective and depends on the
experience and judgment of the Qualified Person
(&#8220;QP&#8221;) calculating the resource estimate. Mr. Sandefur, QP, allowed 
indicated material at Tres Amigos&nbsp;and San
Pablo because of (1) the similarity of the variograms, and (2) the fact of 
recent production by DynaM&eacute;xico from San Pablo
of some 42,000 tonnes mill feed at an average grade of approximately 15 g/t 
(&#8220;grams per tonne&#8221;). &nbsp;Three of the
individual veins at La Purisima satisfied criterion (1) above, but CAM elected 
not to include this material in &#8220;Indicated&#8221;
because of the higher nugget effect at La Purisima, and because there was 
apparently historic underground mining there. This Mineral
Resource Estimate for SJG does not include any ore loss or dilution outside 
wireframes, and as currently defined, is probably
most appropriate for a highly selective, small equipment underground 
operation.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
veins at San Jose de Gracia have been historically mined for many years and 
historic mined volumes are not available. The one
exception is the approximate 42,000 tonnes of ore processed by DynaM&eacute;xico
during its pilot production activities in 2003-2006.
The resource table is not adjusted for any historic mining. To validate that 
historic mining had not significantly reduced the
resource, CAM reviewed the database for all assays greater than 1 gram per ton 
gold that were next to missing values at the bottom
of drill holes. Only four assays satisfying this criterion were found, and on 
the basis of this review, Mr. Sandefur does not
believe that significant mining has occurred within the volumes defined by the 
wireframes.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; background-
color: white">Servicios
y Proyectos Mineros</FONT><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif"> performed a database review and considers that
a reasonable level of verification has been completed, and that no material 
issues have been left unidentified from the drilling
programs undertaken.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><I>Mineral
Resource Estimate and 43-101 Technical Report - Data Verification--</I>Mr. Ramon
Luna Espinoza (&#8220;Mr. Luna&#8221;) initially
visited the San Jose de Gracia Project in November 2010, and conducted site 
inspections at SJG in November 2011 and January 2012.
Mr. Sandefur conducted a site inspection of the SJG Project in January 2012. 
<FONT STYLE="letter-spacing: -0.15pt">While at the
Property in November 2011, Mr. Luna inspected the areas of Tres Amigos, La 
Prieta, Gossan Cap, San Pablo, La Union, and La Purisima,
and historic mining sites. In January 2012, Mr. Sandefur and Mr. Luna inspected 
the areas of Tres Amigos, San Pablo, La Union,
and La Purisima. Pictures of the areas were taken. Many of the drill pads for
the drilling programs of 2007 to 2011 were clearly
located and identified. Mr. Luna also inspected San Jos&eacute; de 
Gracia&#8217;s core logging and storage facilities, the geology
offices, the meteorological station, the plant nursery, and the mill. Mr. 
Sandefur also inspected San Jos&eacute; de Gracia&#8217;s
core logging and storage facilities.</FONT></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>National
Instrument 43-101 (&#8220;NI 43-101&#8221;) Mineral Resource Estimate for the 
San Jose de Gracia Property (2012)</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Company received from DynaM&eacute;xico on February 14, 2012, a National 
Instrument 43-101 Mineral Resource Estimate for San Jose
de Gracia. The NI 43-101 Resource Estimate (the &#8220;2012 DynaM&eacute;xico-
CAM SJG Mineral Resource Estimate&#8221;, the &#8220;Resource
Estimate&#8221;) was prepared by Mr. Robert Sandefur, BS, MSc, P.E., a Qualified
Person as defined under NI 43-101, and a senior
reserve analyst for Chlumsky, Armbrust &amp; Meyer LLC, Lakewood, CO 
(&#8220;CAM&#8221;). The Resource Estimate concentrates on
four separate main vein systems at SJG: Tres Amigos, San Pablo, La Union, and La
Purisima.</FONT></P>

<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 7.75pt 6pt 0; 
text-align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif"><FONT STYLE="letter-spacing: -0.05pt">&nbsp;</FONT></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>National
Instrument 43-101 Technical Report on the San Jose de Gracia Property 
(2012)</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Company received from DynaM&eacute;xico on March 28, 2012, a National Instrument
43-101 (&#8220;NI 43-101&#8221;) compliant Technical
Report for the San Jose de Gracia Project (the &#8220;2012 DynaM&eacute;xico 
Luna-CAM SJG Technical Report&#8221;, the &#8220;Technical
Report&#8221;), and approved by DynaResource de M&eacute;xico, S.A. de C.V. 
(&#8220;DynaM&eacute;xico&#8221;), the 100% owner
of SJG.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
2012 DynaM&eacute;xico Luna-CAM SJG Technical Report was prepared by Mr. Ramon 
Luna Espinoza, BS, P.Geo., of <FONT STYLE="color: #333333; background-color: 
white">Servicios
y Proyectos Mineros, Hermosillo, M&eacute;xico, and </FONT>a Qualified Person as
defined under NI 43-101; and by Mr. Robert Sandefur,
BS, MSc, P.E., a senior reserve analyst for Chlumsky, Armbrust &amp; Meyer LLC, 
Lakewood, CO., and a Qualified Person as defined
under NI 43-101. The 2012 DynaM&eacute;xico Luna-CAM SJG Technical Report 
includes as Section Fourteen (14) a Mineral Resource
Estimate for SJG as prepared by Mr. Sandefur (the &#8220;2012 DynaM&eacute;xico-
CAM SJG 43-101 Mineral Resource Estimate&#8221;,
the &#8220;Resource Estimate&#8221;).</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Company filed the Technical Report on SEDAR (www.sedar.com) on March 28, 
2012.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Updated
National Instrument 43-101 Technical Report for San Jose de Gracia 
(2012)</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Company received from DynaM&eacute;xico on December 31, 2012, an updated NI 43-
101 compliant Technical Report for the San Jose
de Gracia Project (the &#8220;Updated 2012 DynaM&eacute;xico Luna-CAM SJG 
Technical Report&#8221;). The updated Technical Report
was approved by DynaM&eacute;xico, and filed by the Company on SEDAR on December
31, 2012.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt/13pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>No
Known Reserves</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt/13pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
SJG property is without known reserves. Under U.S. standards, mineralization may
not be classified as a &#8220;reserve&#8221;
unless a determination has been made that the mineralization could be
economically and legally produced or extracted at the time
the reserve determination is made.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Exploitation
Amendment Agreement (&#8220;EAA&#8221;)</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">On
May 15, 2013, DynaMineras entered into an Exploitation Amendment Agreement 
(&#8220;EAA&#8221;) with DynaM&eacute;xico. The EAA
grants to DynaMineras the right to finance, explore, develop and exploit the SJG
Property, in exchange for:</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt 0.2in; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">(a)
Reimbursement of all costs associated with financing, maintenance, exploration, 
development and exploitation of the SJG Property,
which costs are to be charged and billed by DynaMineras to DynaM&eacute;xico; 
and,</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt 0.2in; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">(b)
After Item (A) above, the receipt by DynaMineras of 75% of gross receipts 
received by DynaM&eacute;xico from the sale of all minerals
produced from SJG, to the point that DynaMineras has received 200% of its 
advanced funds; and,</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt 0.2in; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">(c)
after items (A) and (B) above; the receipt by DynaMineras of 50% of all gross 
receipts received by DynaM&eacute;xico from the
sale of all minerals produced from SJG, and throughout the term of the EAA; 
and,</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt 0.2in; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">(d)
in addition to Items (A), (B), and (C) above, DynaMineras shall receive a 2.5% 
NSR (&#8220;Net Smelter Royalty&#8221;) on all
minerals sold from SJG over the term of the EAA.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
total Advances made by DynaMineras to DynaM&eacute;xico as of June 30, 2015 is 
$4,046,138. The EAA is the third and latest Amendment
to the original Contract Mining Services and Mineral Production Agreement (the 
&#8220;Operating Agreement&#8221;), which was previously
entered into by DynaMineras with DynaM&eacute;xico in April 2005, wherein 
DynaMineras was named the Exclusive Operating Entity
at SJG. The Operating Agreement was previously amended in September 2006 (the 
&#8220;First Amendment&#8221;), and amended again
at July 15, 2011 (the &#8220;Second Amendment&#8221;). The Term of the Second 
Amendment is 20 years, and the EAA (Third Amendment)
provides for the continuation of the 20 Year Term from the date of the Second 
Amendment (July 15, 2011).</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt"><FONT 
STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Surface
Rights Agreement</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; letter-spacing: 
-0.1pt">On
January 6, 2014 DynaMineras entered into a 20 year surface rights agreement with
</FONT><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; background-color: 
white">the
Santa Maria Ejido Community surrounding the San Jose de Gracia Property (the 
&#8220;20 Year SRA&#8221;). The 20 Year SRA covers
an area of 4,399 hectares surrounding the main mineral resource areas of SJG, 
and provides for annual lease payments by DynaMineras
of $1,359,443 Pesos (approx. $104,250 USD), commencing in 2014. </FONT><FONT 
STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
20 year SRA provides DynaMineras with surface access to the core resource areas 
of SJG, and allows for all permitted mining, pilot
production and exploration activities from the owners of the surface rights 
(Santa Maria Ejido community).</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; background-
color: white">Additionally,
DynaMineras expects to construct a Medical Facility and a Community Center 
within the SJG community in year 2015. DynaMineras
reports that land and building for which the medical facility and community 
center will be constructed have been approved for
re-zoning by the local community; and plans are being drawn for constructing the
facilities.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif"><B>Rehabilitation
and Start-up of Pilot Mill Facility at San Jose de Gracia</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">Under
the terms of the Exploitation Amendment Agreement (&#8220;EAA&#8221;), as 
described above, DynaMineras has rehabilitated the pilot
mill facility at SJG and it has rehabilitated the San Pablo mine. The SJG pilot 
mill facility (a gravimetric-flotation circuit)
is designed to process bulk samples mined from selected target areas of SJG, 
including San Pablo. Operations at SJG are managed
by DynaMineras, and are projected to be similar to those conducted by 
DynaM&eacute;xico during 2003-2006.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"></P>

<P STYLE="font: 10pt/12pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 5pt; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif"><B>Current
Operations - Test Underground Mining and Pilot Mill Operations</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">Operational
Permits for the rehabilitation of the San Pablo Mine and for the refurbishment 
of the Pilot Mill Facility, including the installation
of the Tailings Pond area adjacent to the pilot mill facility were obtained in 
fall 2013, leading to the rehabilitation of the
San Pablo Mine and the refurbishing of the Pilot Mill Facility in 2014. Pilot 
Production Operations commenced in October 2014,
with approximately 1,650 Oz. Gold being delivered for sale during the startup 
testing phase.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:

expects to continue its test mining and pilot mill production operations in 
2015. (See Preparation for Pilot Production Improvement
and Expansion below.)</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt"><FONT 
STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Preparation
for Pilot Production Improvement and Expansion</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">Subsequent
to the rehabilitation of the San Pablo mine, and subsequent to the refurnishing 
of the Pilot mill facility at SJG, and subsequent
to the initial test mill runs of the pilot mill facility through March 2015, 
DynaMineras is now preparing to improve and expand
its test mining activities and in order to achieve higher volumes of bulk mining
samples to be delivered to the pilot mill facility
for processing. The Company is budgeting approximately $ 2M USD for this 
improvement and expansion program, utilizing the proceeds
from the Golden Post transaction (See &#8220;<B>Financing Agreement with Golden 
Post Rail, LLC, a Texas Limited Liability Company&#8221;,
above).</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Competitive
Advantage</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Company, through its subsidiaries, has been conducting business in M&eacute;xico
since March 2000. During this period the Company
believes it has structured its subsidiaries properly and strategically, and 
during which time the Company has retained key personnel
and developed key relationships and support. The Company believes its experience
and accomplishments and relationships in M&eacute;xico
give it a competitive advantage, even though many competitors may be larger and 
have more capital resources.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif">DynaM&eacute;xico
retains 100% of the rights to concessions over the area of the San Jos&eacute; 
de Gracia property and it currently sees no competition
for mining on the lands covered by those concessions. The sale of gold and any 
bi-products would be subject to global market prices,
which prices fluctuate daily. DynaM&eacute;xico was successful in selling gold 
concentrates produced from SJG in prior years,
and the Company expects a competitive market for produced concentrates and/or 
other mineral products in the future. Actual prices
received by DynaMineras in the sale of concentrates or other products produced 
from San Jose de Gracia would depend upon these
global market prices, less deductions.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
Company&#8217;s operating subsidiaries, DynaMineras and DynaOperaciones, receive
monthly fees for management of the SJG activities
and personnel. These fee amounts are eliminated in consolidation. Other than 
those intercompany fees, the Company reported revenue
of $144,558 and $586,846 for the six months ended June 30, 2015 and 
2014.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Capital
Requirements</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">The
mining industry in general requires significant capital in order to take a 
property from the exploration, to development to production.
These costs remain a significant barrier to entry for the average company but 
once in production, there is a ready market for
the final products, In the case of SJG, the final product would be mainly gold, 
the price of which is determined by global markets,
so there is not a dependence on a customer base.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif"><B>Gold</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><I>Gold
Uses.</I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Gold generally is used for fabrication or 
investment. Fabricated gold has a variety of end uses,
including jewelry, electronics, dentistry, industrial and decorative uses, 
medals, medallions and official coins. Gold investors
buy gold bullion, official coins and jewelry.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><I>Gold
Supply.</I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;A combination of current mine production, 
recycling and draw-down of existing gold stocks held
by governments, financial institutions, industrial organizations and private 
individuals make up the annual gold supply. Based
on public information available for the years 2008 through 2014, on average, 
current mine production has accounted for approximately
64% of the annual gold supply.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><I>Gold
Price.</I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The following table presents the annual high, 
low and average daily afternoon fixing prices
for gold over the past ten years on the London Bullion Market 
($/ounce):</FONT></P>

<P STYLE="font: 1pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0; text-indent: 
0.5in"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 6pt 0"><FONT 
STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">Source:
Kitco, Reuters and the London Bullion Market Association</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt"><FONT 
STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">On
August 12, 2015, the afternoon fixing gold price on the London Bullion Market 
was $1,119 per ounce and the spot market gold price
on the New York Commodity Exchange was $1,123 per ounce.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Condition
of Physical Assets and Insurance</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">Our
business is capital intensive and requires ongoing capital investment for the 
replacement, modernization or expansion of equipment
and facilities. We and our subsidiaries maintain insurance policies against 
property loss. Such insurance, however, contains exclusions
and limitations on coverage, particularly with respect to environmental 
liability and political risk. There can be no assurance
that claims would be paid under such insurance policies in connection with a 
particular event.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt"><FONT 
STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Environmental
Matters</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">Our
activities are largely outside the United States and subject to governmental 
regulations for the protection of the environment.
We conduct our operations so as to protect public health and the environment and
believe our operations are in compliance with
applicable laws and regulations in all material respects. DynaM&eacute;xico is 
involved with maintaining tailings ponds and test
mining and pilot production activities (through DynaMineras) with the oversight 
of SEMARNAT, the federal environmental agency
of M&eacute;xico.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt"><FONT 
STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif"><B>Results
for the Three and Six Months Ended June 30, 2015 and 2014</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt/13pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">In
2013, the Company was focused on obtaining operational permits and raising 
funds, in order to prepare for rehabilitation of the
San Pablo mine and refurbishing the pilot mill facility at SJG; and preparing to
install the tailings pond adjacent to the pilot
mill facility. Operational permits were obtained in fall 2013, leading to the 
rehabilitation of the San Pablo Mine and the refurbishing
of the Pilot Mill Facility.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt/13pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">In
the second quarter 2014, DynaMineras commenced test mining and pilot mill 
operations at San Jose de Gracia. Further rehabilitation
of the San Pablo mine and the tailings pond area adjacent to the pilot mill 
facility continued into the fourth quarter. The rehabilitation
of the San Pablo mine included driving ramps and building access to the high 
grade areas of San Pablo as defined by core drill
holes.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt/13pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-
align: justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, 
Serif">Throughout
the year 2014, the test pilot operations have yielded the underground mining and
mill processing of approx. 8,841 tonnes of material,
the production of approximately 1,676 gross oz. au (and net of buyer&#8217;s 
price discount and refining costs approximately 1438
oz au) of gold-silver concentrates, and the receipt of $1,476,188 in revenues 
from the sale of gold-silver products from Dore
and gravity-flotation concentrates. Throughout the year DynaMineras was active 
in rehabilitating and developing the San Pablo
Mine and refurbishing the Pilot Mill Facility and generally preparing to 
commence pilot production operations.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">For
the six months ended June 30, 2015, the test pilot operations have yielded the 
production of an estimated 150 Oz gold from mill
runs completed over a 10 day period in January, from approximately 900 tons of
mineralized feed material which was processed through
the gravity and flotation circuit of the Pilot Mill Facility at SJG. DynaMineras
further reports the estimated amount of tailings
remaining from the previous test mill runs utilizing only the gravity 
concentration circuit, and which material will be re-processed
through the flotation circuit, is approximately 3,000 Tons. Internal assays 
report: (a) an average feed grade for the mill runs
during January 2015 of approximately 8 g/t Au; and, (b) an average grade for the
mineralized material to be re-processed (gravity
tailings, from early test runs in mid 2014) of approximately 6 g/t Au. And, 
DynaMineras further reports mined inventory of approximately
1,000 tons, available for processing through the pilot mill facility, and 
approximately 15 tons of gold concentrates available
for delivery and sale.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"><FONT STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif">REVENUE.
Revenues for the six months ended June 30, 2015 and 2014 were $144,558 and 
$586,846, respectively. The Company commenced test
mining and initial test runs of the pilot mill facility in the 2<SUP>nd</SUP> 
quarter of 2014. Revenues for the three months ended
June 30, 2015 and 2014 were $0 and $586,846, respectively. In the current 
quarter, the Company was engaged in the final stages
of mine and mill preparation and improvements to operations in order to commence
and sustain consistent test mining and milling
operations, and in closing financing agreements in which to fund consistent 
operations.</FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0 0 6pt; text-align:
justify"></P>
